**v10** A rebuke cuts into a man of discernmentdeeper than a hundred lashes cut into a fool.

**v11** An evil man seeks only rebellion; a cruel messenger will be sent against him.

**v12** It is better to meet a bear robbed of her cubsthan a fool in his folly.

**v13** If anyone returns evil for good, evil will never leave his house.

**v14** To start a quarrel is to release a flood; so abandon the dispute before it breaks out.

**v15** Acquitting the guilty and condemning the righteous—both are detestable to the LORD.

**v16** Why should the fool have money in his handwith no intention of buying wisdom?

**v17** A friend loves at all times, and a brother is born for adversity.

**v18** A man lacking judgment strikes hands in pledgeand puts up security for his neighbor.

**v19** He who loves transgression loves strife; he who builds his gate high invites destruction.

**v20** The one with a perverse heart finds no good, and he whose tongue is deceitful falls into trouble.

**v21** A man fathers a fool to his own grief; the father of a fool has no joy.

**v22** A joyful heart is good medicine, but a broken spirit dries up the bones.

**v23** A wicked man takes a covert bribe [^2] to subvert the course of justice.

**v24** Wisdom is the focus of the discerning, but the eyes of a fool wander to the ends of the earth.

**v25** A foolish son brings grief to his fatherand bitterness to her who bore him.

**v26** It is surely not good to punish the innocentor to flog a noble for his honesty.

**v27** A man of knowledge restrains his words, and a man of understanding maintains a calm spirit.

**v28** Even a fool is considered wise if he keeps silent, and discerning when he holds his tongue.
[^1]: Or sacrifices ( 17:1)
[^2]: Hebrew a bribe from the bosom ( 17:23)

### Chapter 18

#### The Selfishness of the Unfriendly
**v1** He who isolates himself pursues selfish desires; he rebels against all sound judgment.

**v2** A fool does not delight in understanding, but only in airing his opinions.

**v3** With a wicked man comes contempt as well, and shame is accompanied by disgrace.

**v4** The words of a man's mouth are deep waters; the fountain of wisdom is a bubbling brook.

**v5** Showing partiality [^1] to the wicked is not good, nor is depriving the innocent of justice.

**v6** A fool's lips bring him strife, and his mouth invites a beating.

**v7** A fool's mouth is his ruin, and his lips are a snare to his soul.

**v8** The words of a gossip are like choice morselsthat go down into the inmost being.

**v9** Whoever is slothful in his workis brother to him who destroys.

**v10** The name of the LORD is a strong tower; the righteous run to it [^2] and are safe.

**v11** A rich man's wealth is his fortified city; it is like a high wall in his imagination.

**v12** Before his downfall a man's heart is proud, but humility comes before honor.

**v13** He who answers a matter before he hears it—this is folly and disgrace to him.

**v14** The spirit of a man can endure his sickness, but who can survive a broken spirit?

**v15** The heart of the discerning acquires knowledge, and the ear of the wise seeks it out.

**v16** A man's gift opens doors for him, and brings him before great men.

**v17** The first to state his case seems rightuntil another comes and cross-examines him.

**v18** Casting the lot ends quarrelsand separates strong opponents.

**v19** An offended brother is harder to win than a fortified city, and disputes are like the bars of a castle.

**v20** From the fruit of his mouth a man's belly is filled; with the harvest from his lips he is satisfied.

**v21** Life and death are in the power of the tongue, and those who love it will eat its fruit.

**v22** He who finds a wife finds a good thingand obtains favor from the LORD.

**v23** The poor man pleads for mercy, but the rich man answers harshly.

**v24** A man of many companions may come to ruin, but there is a friend who stays closer than a brother.
[^1]: Hebrew Lifting the face ( 18:5)
[^2]: Or to Him ( 18:10)

### Chapter 19

#### The Man of Integrity
**v1** Better a poor man who walks with integritythan a fool whose lips are perverse.

**v2** Even zeal is no good without knowledge, and he who hurries his footsteps misses the mark.

**v3** A man's own folly subverts his way, yet his heart rages against the LORD.

**v4** Wealth attracts many friends, but a poor man is deserted by his friend.

**v5** A false witness will not go unpunished, and one who utters lies will not escape.

**v6** Many seek the favor of the prince, and everyone is a friend of the gift giver.

**v7** All the brothers of a poor man hate him—how much more do his friends avoid him!He may pursue them with pleading, but they are nowhere to be found.

**v8** He who acquires wisdom loves himself; one who safeguards understanding will find success.

**v9** A false witness will not go unpunished, and one who pours out lies will perish.

**v10** Luxury is unseemly for a fool—how much worse for a slave to rule over princes!

**v11** A man's insight gives him patience, and his virtue is to overlook an offense.

**v12** A king's rage is like the roar of a lion, but his favor is like dew on the grass.

**v13** A foolish son is his father's ruin, and a quarrelsome wife is like a constant dripping.

**v14** Houses and wealth are inherited from fathers, but a prudent wife is from the LORD.

**v15** Laziness brings on deep sleep, and an idle soul will suffer hunger.

**v16** He who keeps a commandment preserves his soul, but he who is careless in his ways will die.

**v17** Kindness to the poor is a loan to the LORD, and He will repay the lender.

**v18** Discipline your son, for in that there is hope; do not be party to his death.

**v19** A man of great anger must pay the penalty; if you rescue him, you will have to do so again.

**v20** Listen to counsel and accept discipline, that you may be wise the rest of your days.

**v21** Many plans are in a man's heart, but the purpose of the LORD will prevail.

**v22** The desire of a man is loving devotion; better to be poor than a liar.

**v23** The fear of the LORD leads to life, that one may rest content, without visitation from harm.

**v24** The slacker buries his hand in the dish; he will not even bring it back to his mouth.

**v25** Strike a mocker, and the simple will beware; rebuke the discerning man, and he will gain knowledge.

**v26** He who assaults his father or evicts his motheris a son who brings shame and disgrace.

**v27** If you cease to hear instruction, my son, you will stray from the words of knowledge.

**v28** A corrupt witness mocks justice, and a wicked mouth swallows iniquity.

**v29** Judgments are prepared for mockers, and beatings for the backs of fools.
### Chapter 20

#### Wine Is a Mocker
**v1** Wine is a mocker, strong drink is a brawler, and whoever is led astray by them is not wise.

**v2** The terror of a king is like the roar of a lion; whoever provokes him forfeits his own life. [^1]

**v3** It is honorable for a man to resolve a dispute, but any fool will quarrel.

**v4** The slacker does not plow in season; at harvest time he looks, but nothing is there.

**v5** The intentions of a man's heart are deep waters, but a man of understanding draws them out.

**v6** Many a man proclaims his loving devotion, but who can find a trustworthy man?

**v7** The righteous man walks with integrity; blessed are his children after him.

**v8** A king who sits on a throne to judgesifts out all evil with his eyes.

**v9** Who can say, "I have kept my heart pure; I am cleansed from my sin"?

**v10** Differing weights and unequal measures [^2]—both are detestable to the LORD.

**v11** Even a young man is known by his actions—whether his conduct is pure and upright.

**v12** Ears that hear and eyes that see—the LORD has made them both.

**v13** Do not love sleep, or you will grow poor; open your eyes, and you will have plenty of food.

**v14** "Worthless, worthless!" says the buyer, but on the way out, he gloats.

**v15** There is an abundance of gold and rubies, but lips of knowledge are a rare treasure.

**v16** Take the garment of the one who posts security for a stranger; get collateral if it is for a foreigner. [^3]

**v17** Food gained by fraud is sweet to a man, but later his mouth is full of gravel.

**v18** Set plans by consultation, and wage war under sound guidance.

**v19** He who reveals secrets is a constant gossip; avoid the one who babbles [^4] with his lips.

**v20** Whoever curses his father or mother, his lamp will be extinguished in deepest darkness.

**v21** An inheritance gained quicklywill not be blessed in the end.

**v22** Do not say, "I will avenge this evil!" Wait on the LORD, and He will save you.

**v23** Unequal weights are detestable to the LORD, and dishonest scales are no good.

**v24** A man's steps are from the LORD, so how can anyone understand his own way?

**v25** It is a trap for a man to dedicate something rashly, only later to reconsider his vows.

**v26** A wise king separates out the wickedand drives the threshing wheel over them.

**v27** The spirit [^5] of a man is the lamp of the LORD, searching out his inmost being.

**v28** Loving devotion and faithfulness preserve a king; by these he maintains his throne.

**v29** The glory of young men is their strength, and gray hair is the splendor of the old.

**v30** Lashes and wounds scour evil, and beatings cleanse the inmost parts.
[^1]: Literally sins against his own soul ( 20:2)
[^2]: Hebrew A stone and a stone, an ephah and an ephah ( 20:10)
[^3]: Or a wayward woman ( 20:16)
[^4]: Or the one who is simple ( 20:19)
[^5]: Or breath or speech ( 20:27)

### Chapter 21

#### The King's Heart
**v1** The king's heart is a waterway in the hand of the LORD; He directs it where He pleases.

**v2** All a man's ways seem right to him, but the LORD weighs the heart.

**v3** To do righteousness and justiceis more desirable to the LORD than sacrifice.

**v4** Haughty eyes and a proud heart—the guides of the wicked—are sin.

**v5** The plans of the diligent bring plenty, as surely as haste leads to poverty.

**v6** Making a fortune by a lying tongueis a vanishing mist, a deadly pursuit.

**v7** The violence of the wicked will sweep them awaybecause they refuse to do what is just.

**v8** The way of a guilty man is crooked, but the conduct of the innocent is upright.

**v9** Better to live on a corner of the roofthan to share a house with a quarrelsome wife.

**v10** The soul of the wicked man craves evil; his neighbor finds no favor in his eyes.

**v11** When a mocker is punished, the simple gain wisdom; and when a wise man is instructed, he acquires knowledge.

**v12** The Righteous One [^1] considers the house of the wickedand brings the wicked to ruin.

**v13** Whoever shuts his ears to the cry of the poor, he too shall cry out and receive no answer.

**v14** A gift in secret soothes anger, and a covert bribe [^2] pacifies great wrath.

**v15** Justice executed is a joy to the righteous, but a terror to the workers of iniquity.

**v16** The man who strays from the path of understandingwill rest in the assembly of the dead.

**v17** He who loves pleasure will become poor; the one who loves wine and oil will never be rich.

**v18** The wicked become a ransom for the righteous, and the faithless for the upright.

**v19** Better to live in the desertthan with a contentious and ill-tempered wife.

**v20** Precious treasures and oil are in the dwelling of the wise, but a foolish man consumes them.

**v21** He who pursues righteousness and loving devotionfinds life, righteousness, and honor.

**v22** A wise man scales the city of the mightyand pulls down the stronghold in which they trust.

**v23** He who guards his mouth and tonguekeeps his soul from distress.

**v24** Mocker is the name of the proud and arrogant man—of him who acts with excessive pride.

**v25** The craving of the slacker kills himbecause his hands refuse to work.
**v26** All day long he covets more, but the righteous give without restraint.

**v27** The sacrifice of the wicked is detestable—how much more so when brought with ill intent!

**v28** A lying witness will perish, but the man who listens to truth will speak forever.

**v29** A wicked man hardens his face, [^3] but the upright man makes his way sure.

**v30** There is no wisdom, no understanding, no counselthat can prevail against the LORD.

**v31** A horse is prepared for the day of battle, but victory is of the LORD.
[^1]: Or The righteous one ( 21:12)
[^2]: Hebrew a bribe in the bosom ( 21:14)
[^3]: Or puts up a bold front ( 21:29)

### Chapter 22

#### A Good Name
**v1** A good name is more desirable than great riches; favor is better than silver and gold.

**v2** The rich and the poor have this in common:The LORD is Maker of them all.

**v3** The prudent see danger and take cover, but the simple keep going and suffer the consequences.

**v4** The rewards of humility and the fear of the LORDare wealth and honor and life.

**v5** Thorns and snares lie on the path of the perverse; he who guards his soul stays far from them.

**v6** Train up a child in the way he should go, and when he is old he will not depart from it.

**v7** The rich rule over the poor, and the borrower is slave to the lender.

**v8** He who sows injustice will reap disaster, and the rod of his fury will be destroyed. [^1]

**v9** A generous man [^2] will be blessed, for he shares his bread with the poor.

**v10** Drive out the mocker, and conflict will depart; even quarreling and insults will cease.

**v11** He who loves a pure heart and gracious lipswill have the king for a friend.

**v12** The LORD's eyes keep watch over knowledge, but He frustrates the words of the faithless.

**v13** The slacker says, "There is a lion outside!I will be slain in the streets!"

**v14** The mouth of an adulteress is a deep pit; he who is under the wrath of the LORD will fall into it.

**v15** Foolishness is bound up in the heart of a child, but the rod of discipline drives it far from him.

**v16** Oppressing the poor to enrich oneself or giving gifts to the richwill surely lead to poverty.
#### Thirty Sayings of the Wise
#### Saying 1

**v17** Incline your ear and hear the words of the wise—apply your mind to my knowledge—
**v18** for it is pleasing when you keep them within you and they are constantly on your lips.
**v19** So that your trust may be in the LORD, I instruct you today—yes, you.
**v20** Have I not written for you thirty sayings [^3] about counsel and knowledge,
**v21** to show you true and reliable words, that you may soundly answer those who sent you?
#### Saying 2

**v22** Do not rob a poor man because he is poor, and do not crush the afflicted at the gate,
**v23** for the LORD will take up their caseand will plunder those who rob them.
#### Saying 3

**v24** Do not make friends with an angry man, and do not associate with a hot-tempered man,
**v25** or you may learn his waysand entangle yourself in a snare.
#### Saying 4

**v26** Do not be one who gives pledges, who puts up security for debts.
**v27** If you have nothing with which to pay, why should your bed be taken from under you?
#### Saying 5

**v28** Do not move an ancient boundary stonewhich your fathers have placed.
#### Saying 6

**v29** Do you see a man skilled in his work?He will be stationed in the presence of kings; he will not stand before obscure men.
[^1]: LXX includes God blesses a cheerful and generous man, but foolish works will come to an end; see also 2 Corinthians 9:7. ( 22:8)
[^2]: Literally He whose eye is good ( 22:9)
[^3]: Or written for you excellent sayings or written for you three times ( 22:20)

### Chapter 23

#### True Riches
#### Saying 7

**v1** When you sit down to dine with a ruler, consider carefully what is set before you, [^1]
**v2** and put a knife to your throatif you possess a great appetite.
**v3** Do not crave his delicacies, for that food is deceptive.
#### Saying 8

**v4** Do not wear yourself out to get rich; be wise enough to restrain yourself.
**v5** When you glance at wealth, it disappears, for it makes wings for itselfand flies like an eagle to the sky.
#### Saying 9

**v6** Do not eat the bread of a stingy man, [^2] and do not crave his delicacies;
**v7** for he is keeping track, inwardly counting the cost. [^3]"Eat and drink," he says to you, but his heart is not with you.
**v8** You will vomit up what little you have eatenand waste your pleasant words.
#### Saying 10

**v9** Do not speak to a fool, for he will despise the wisdom of your words.
#### Saying 11

**v10** Do not move an ancient boundary stoneor encroach on the fields of the fatherless,
**v11** for their Redeemer is strong; He will take up their case against you.
#### Saying 12

**v12** Apply your heart to instructionand your ears to words of knowledge.
#### Saying 13

**v13** Do not withhold discipline from a child; although you strike him with a rod, he will not die.
**v14** Strike him with a rod, and you will deliver his soul from Sheol.
#### Saying 14

**v15** My son, if your heart is wise, my own heart will indeed rejoice.
**v16** My inmost being [^4] will rejoicewhen your lips speak what is right.
#### Saying 15

**v17** Do not let your heart envy sinners, but always continue in the fear of the LORD.
**v18** For surely there is a future, and your hope will not be cut off.
#### Saying 16

**v19** Listen, my son, and be wise, and guide your heart on the right course.
**v20** Do not join those who drink too much wineor gorge themselves on meat.
**v21** For the drunkard and the glutton will come to poverty, and drowsiness will clothe them in rags.
#### Saying 17

**v22** Listen to your father who gave you life, and do not despise your mother when she is old.
**v23** Invest in truth and never sell it—in wisdom and instruction and understanding.
**v24** The father of a righteous man will greatly rejoice, and he who fathers a wise son will delight in him.
**v25** May your father and mother be glad, and may she who gave you birth rejoice!
#### Saying 18

**v26** My son, give me your heart, and let your eyes delight in my ways.
**v27** For a prostitute is a deep pit, and an adulteress [^5] is a narrow well.
**v28** Like a robber she lies in waitand multiplies the faithless among men.
#### Saying 19

**v29** Who has woe? Who has sorrow?Who has contentions? Who has complaints?Who has needless wounds? Who has bloodshot eyes?
**v30** Those who linger over wine, who go to taste mixed drinks.
**v31** Do not gaze at wine while it is red, when it sparkles in the cupand goes down smoothly.
**v32** In the end it bites like a snakeand stings like a viper.
**v33** Your eyes will see strange things, and your mind will utter perversities.
**v34** You will be like one sleeping on the high seasor lying on the top of a mast:
**v35** "They struck me, but I feel no pain!They beat me, but I did not know it!When can I wake upto search for another drink?"
[^1]: Or who is before you ( 23:1)
[^2]: Literally of him whose eye is evil ( 23:6)
[^3]: Or for as he calculates in his soul, so is he ( 23:7)
[^4]: Hebrew My kidneys ( 23:16)
[^5]: Or a foreign woman or a wayward wife ( 23:27)

### Chapter 24

#### Do Not Envy
#### Saying 20

**v1** Do not envy wicked menor desire their company;
**v2** for their hearts devise violence, and their lips declare trouble.
#### Saying 21

**v3** By wisdom a house is builtand by understanding it is established;
**v4** through knowledge its rooms are filledwith every precious and beautiful treasure.
#### Saying 22

**v5** A wise man is strong, [^1] and a man of knowledge enhances his strength.
**v6** Only with sound guidance should you wage war, and victory lies in a multitude of counselors.
#### Saying 23

**v7** Wisdom is too high for a fool; he does not open his mouth in the meeting place.
#### Saying 24

**v8** He who plots evilwill be called a schemer.
**v9** A foolish scheme is sin, and a mocker is detestable to men.
#### Saying 25

**v10** If you faint in the day of distress, how small is your strength!
**v11** Rescue those being led away to death, and restrain those stumbling toward the slaughter.
**v12** If you say, "Behold, we did not know about this,"does not He who weighs hearts consider it?Does not the One who guards your life know?Will He not repay a man according to his deeds?
#### Saying 26

**v13** Eat honey, my son, for it is good, and the honeycomb is sweet to your taste.
**v14** Know therefore that wisdom is sweet to your soul.If you find it, there is a future for you, and your hope will never be cut off.
#### Saying 27

**v15** Do not lie in wait, O wicked man, near the dwelling of the righteous; do not destroy his resting place.
**v16** For though a righteous man may fall seven times, he still gets up; but the wicked stumble in bad times.
#### Saying 28

**v17** Do not gloat when your enemy falls, and do not let your heart rejoice when he stumbles,
**v18** or the LORD will see and disapprove, and turn His wrath away from him.
#### Saying 29

**v19** Do not fret over evildoers, and do not be envious of the wicked.
**v20** For the evil man has no future; the lamp of the wicked will be extinguished.
#### Saying 30

**v21** My son, fear the LORD and the king, and do not associate with the rebellious.
**v22** For they will bring sudden destruction.Who knows what ruin they can bring?
#### Further Sayings of the Wise

**v23** These also are sayings of the wise:To show partiality in judgmentis not good.
**v24** Whoever tells the guilty, "You are innocent"—peoples will curse him, and nations will denounce him;
**v25** but it will go well with those who convict the guilty, and rich blessing will come upon them.

**v26** An honest answer givenis like a kiss on the lips.

**v27** Complete your outdoor work and prepare your field; after that, you may build your house.

**v28** Do not testify against your neighbor without cause, and do not deceive with your lips.
**v29** Do not say, "I will do to him as he has done to me; I will repay the man according to his work."

**v30** I went past the field of a slackerand by the vineyard of a man lacking judgment.
**v31** Thorns had grown up everywhere, thistles had covered the ground, and the stone wall was broken down.
**v32** I observed and took it to heart; I looked and received instruction:
**v33** A little sleep, a little slumber, a little folding of the hands to rest,
**v34** and poverty will come upon you like a robber, and need like a bandit.
[^1]: LXX The wise are mightier than the strong ( 24:5)

### Chapter 25

#### More Proverbs of Solomon
**v1** These are additional proverbs of Solomon, which were copied by the men of Hezekiah king of Judah:

**v2** It is the glory of God to conceal a matterand the glory of kings to search it out.
**v3** As the heavens are high and the earth is deep, so the hearts of kings cannot be searched.

**v4** Remove the dross from the silver, and a vessel for a silversmith will come forth.
**v5** Remove the wicked from the king's presence, and his throne will be established in righteousness.

**v6** Do not exalt yourself in the presence of the king, and do not stand in the place of great men;
**v7** for it is better to be told, "Come up here!"than to be demoted in the presence of the prince.Even what [^1] you have seen with your own eyes,
**v8** do not bring hastily to court.Otherwise, what will you do in the endwhen your neighbor puts you to shame?

**v9** Argue your case with your neighborwithout betraying another's confidence,
**v10** lest he who hears you bring shame upon you, and your infamy never go away.

**v11** A word fitly spokenis like apples of gold in settings of silver.
**v12** Like an earring of gold or an ornament of fine goldis a wise man's rebuke to a listening ear.

**v13** Like the cold of snow in the time of harvestis a trustworthy messenger to those who send him; he refreshes the soul of his masters.

**v14** Like clouds and wind without rainis the man who boasts of gifts never given.

**v15** Through patience a ruler can be persuaded, and a gentle tongue can break a bone.

**v16** If you find honey, eat just what you need, lest you have too much and vomit it up.

**v17** Seldom set foot in your neighbor's house, lest he grow weary and hate you.

**v18** Like a club or sword or sharp arrowis a man who bears false witness against his neighbor.

**v19** Like a broken tooth or a foot out of jointis confidence in a faithless man in time of trouble.

**v20** Like one who removes a garment on a cold dayor vinegar poured on a wound [^2] is one who sings songs to a heavy heart.

**v21** If your enemy is hungry, give him food to eat, and if he is thirsty, give him water to drink.
**v22** For in so doing, you will heap burning coals on his head, [^3] and the LORD will reward you.

**v23** As the north wind brings forth rain, so a backbiting tongue brings angry looks.

**v24** Better to live on a corner of the roofthan to share a house with a quarrelsome wife.

**v25** Like cold water to a weary soulis good news from a distant land.

**v26** Like a muddied spring or a polluted wellis a righteous man who gives way to the wicked.

**v27** It is not good to eat too much honeyor to search out one's own glory.

**v28** Like a city whose walls are broken downis a man who does not control his temper.
[^1]: Or Even the one ( 25:7)
[^2]: Or on soda ( 25:20)
[^3]: LXX; Hebrew For you will heap burning coals on his head; cited in Romans 12:20 ( 25:22)

### Chapter 26

#### Similitudes and Instructions
**v1** Like snow in summer and rain at harvest, honor does not befit a fool.
**v2** Like a fluttering sparrow or darting swallow, an undeserved curse does not come to rest.
**v3** A whip for the horse, a bridle for the donkey, and a rod for the backs of fools!
**v4** Do not answer a fool according to his folly, or you yourself will be like him.
**v5** Answer a fool according to his folly, lest he become wise in his own eyes.
**v6** Like cutting off one's own feet or drinking violenceis the sending of a message by the hand of a fool.
**v7** Like lame legs hanging limpis a proverb in the mouth of a fool.
**v8** Like binding a stone into a slingis the giving of honor to a fool.
**v9** Like a thorn that goes into the hand of a drunkardis a proverb in the mouth of a fool.
**v10** Like an archer who wounds at randomis he who hires a fool or passerby.
**v11** As a dog returns to its vomit, [^1] so a fool repeats his folly.
**v12** Do you see a man who is wise in his own eyes?There is more hope for a fool than for him.

**v13** The slacker says, "A lion is in the road!A fierce lion roams the public square!"
**v14** As a door turns on its hinges, so the slacker turns on his bed.
**v15** The slacker buries his hand in the dish; it wearies him to bring it back to his mouth.
**v16** The slacker is wiser in his own eyesthan seven men who answer discreetly.

**v17** Like one who grabs a dog by the earsis a passerby who meddles in a quarrel not his own.
**v18** Like a madman shooting firebrandsand deadly arrows,
**v19** so is the man who deceives his neighborand says, "I was only joking!"

**v20** Without wood, a fire goes out; without gossip, a conflict ceases.
**v21** Like charcoal for embers and wood for fire, so is a quarrelsome man for kindling strife.
**v22** The words of a gossip are like choice morselsthat go down into the inmost being.

**v23** Like glaze covering an earthen vesselare burning [^2] lips and a wicked heart.
**v24** A hateful man disguises himself with his speech, but he lays up deceit in his heart.
**v25** When he speaks graciously, do not believe him, for seven abominations fill his heart.
**v26** Though his hatred is concealed by deception, his wickedness will be exposed in the assembly.
**v27** He who digs a pit will fall into it, and he who rolls a stone will have it roll back on him.
**v28** A lying tongue hates those it crushes, and a flattering mouth causes ruin.
[^1]: Cited in 2 Peter 2:22 ( 26:11)
[^2]: Hebrew; LXX smooth ( 26:23)

### Chapter 27

#### Do Not Boast about Tomorrow
**v1** Do not boast about tomorrow, for you do not know what a day may bring.

**v2** Let another praise you, and not your own mouth—a stranger, and not your own lips.

**v3** A stone is heavy and sand is a burden, but aggravation from a fool outweighs them both.

**v4** Wrath is cruel and anger is like a flood, but who can withstand jealousy?

**v5** Better an open rebukethan love that is concealed.

**v6** The wounds of a friend are faithful, but the kisses of an enemy are deceitful.

**v7** The soul that is full loathes honey, but to a hungry soul, any bitter thing is sweet.

**v8** Like a bird that strays from its nestis a man who wanders from his home.

**v9** Oil and incense bring joy to the heart, and the counsel of a friend is sweetness to the soul.

**v10** Do not forsake your friend or your father's friend, and do not go to your brother's housein the day of your calamity; better a neighbor nearbythan a brother far away.

**v11** Be wise, my son, and bring joy to my heart, so that I can answer him who taunts me.

**v12** The prudent see danger and take cover, but the simple keep going and pay the penalty.

**v13** Take the garment of him who posts security for a stranger; get collateral if it is for a foreigner. [^1]

**v14** If one blesses his neighbor with a loud voice early in the morning, it will be counted to him as a curse.

**v15** A constant dripping on a rainy dayand a contentious woman are alike—
**v16** restraining her is like holding back the windor grasping oil with one's right hand.

**v17** As iron sharpens iron, so one man sharpens another. [^2]

**v18** Whoever tends a fig tree will eat its fruit, and he who looks after his master will be honored.

**v19** As water reflects the face, so the heart reflects the true man.

**v20** Sheol and Abaddon [^3] are never satisfied; so the eyes of man are never satisfied.

**v21** A crucible for silver and a furnace for gold, but a man is tested by the praise accorded him.

**v22** Though you grind a fool like grain with mortar and a pestle, yet his folly will not depart from him.

**v23** Be sure to know the state of your flocks, and pay close attention to your herds;
**v24** for riches are not forever, nor does a crown endure to every generation.
**v25** When hay is removed and new growth appearsand the grass from the hills is gathered,
**v26** the lambs will provide you with clothing, and the goats with the price of a field.
**v27** You will have plenty of goats' milk to feed you—food for your householdand nourishment for your maidservants.
[^1]: Or a wayward woman ( 27:13)
[^2]: Hebrew sharpens the face of another or sharpens the countenance of a friend ( 27:17)
[^3]: Or Death and Destruction ( 27:20)

### Chapter 28

#### The Boldness of the Righteous
**v1** The wicked flee when no one pursues, but the righteous are as bold as a lion.

**v2** A land in rebellion has many rulers, but a man of understanding and knowledge maintains order.

**v3** A destitute leader who oppresses the pooris like a driving rain that leaves no food.

**v4** Those who forsake the law praise the wicked, but those who keep the law resist them.

**v5** Evil men do not understand justice, but those who seek the LORD comprehend fully.

**v6** Better a poor man who walks with integritythan a rich man whose ways are perverse.

**v7** A discerning son keeps the law, but a companion of gluttons disgraces his father.

**v8** He who increases his wealth by interest and usurylays it up for one who is kind to the poor.

**v9** Whoever turns his ear away from hearing the law, even his prayer is detestable.

**v10** He who leads the upright along the path of evil will fall into his own pit, but the blameless will inherit what is good.

**v11** A rich man is wise in his own eyes, but a poor man with discernment sees through him.

**v12** When the righteous triumph, there is great glory, but when the wicked rise, men hide themselves.

**v13** He who conceals his sins will not prosper, but whoever confesses and renounces them will find mercy.

**v14** Blessed is the man who is always reverent, [^1] but he who hardens his heart falls into trouble.

**v15** Like a roaring lion or a charging bearis a wicked ruler over a helpless people.

**v16** A leader who lacks judgment is also a great oppressor, but he who hates dishonest profit will prolong his days.

**v17** A man burdened by bloodguilt will flee into the Pit; [^2] let no one support him.

**v18** He who walks with integrity will be kept safe, but whoever is perverse in his ways will suddenly fall.

**v19** The one who works his land will have plenty of food, but whoever chases fantasies will have his fill of poverty.

**v20** A faithful man will abound with blessings, but one eager to be rich will not go unpunished.

**v21** To show partiality is not good, yet a man will do wrong for a piece of bread.

**v22** A stingy man [^3] hastens after wealthand does not know that poverty awaits him.

**v23** He who rebukes a man will later find more favorthan one who flatters with his tongue.

**v24** He who robs his father or mother, saying, "It is not wrong,"is a companion to the man who destroys.

**v25** A greedy man stirs up strife, but he who trusts in the LORD will prosper.

**v26** He who trusts in himself is a fool, but one who walks in wisdom will be safe.

**v27** Whoever gives to the poor will not be in need, but he who hides his eyes will receive many curses.

**v28** When the wicked come to power, people hide themselves; but when they perish, the righteous flourish.
[^1]: Or always fears the LORD; Hebrew does not include the LORD. ( 28:14)
[^2]: Or will be a fugitive until death ( 28:17)
[^3]: Hebrew A man whose eye is evil ( 28:22)

### Chapter 29

#### The Flourishing of the Righteous
**v1** A man who remains stiff-necked after much reproofwill suddenly be shattered beyond recovery.

**v2** When the righteous flourish, the people rejoice, but when the wicked rule, the people groan.

**v3** A man who loves wisdom brings joy to his father, but a companion of prostitutes squanders his wealth.

**v4** By justice a king brings stability to the land, but a man who exacts tribute [^1] demolishes it.

**v5** A man who flatters his neighborspreads a net for his feet.

**v6** An evil man is caught by his own sin, but a righteous one sings and rejoices.

**v7** The righteous consider the cause of the poor, but the wicked have no regard for such concerns.

**v8** Mockers inflame a city, but the wise turn away anger.

**v9** If a wise man goes to court with a fool, there will be raving and laughing with no resolution.

**v10** Men of bloodshed hate a blameless man, but the upright care for his life. [^2]

**v11** A fool vents all his anger, but a wise man holds it back.

**v12** If a ruler listens to lies, all his officials will be wicked.

**v13** The poor man and the oppressor have this in common:The LORD gives light to the eyes of both.

**v14** A king who judges the poor with fairness—his throne will be established forever.

**v15** A rod of correction imparts wisdom, but a child left to himself disgraces his mother.

**v16** When the wicked thrive, rebellion increases; but the righteous will see their downfall.

**v17** Discipline your son, and he will give you rest; he will bring delight to your soul.

**v18** Where there is no vision, the people cast off restraint; but blessed is he who keeps the Law.

**v19** A servant cannot be corrected by words alone; though he understands, he will not respond.

**v20** Do you see a man who speaks in haste?There is more hope for a fool than for him.

**v21** A servant pampered from his youthwill bring grief in the end.

**v22** An angry man stirs up dissension, and a hot-tempered man abounds in transgression.

**v23** A man's pride will bring him low, but a humble spirit will obtain honor.

**v24** A partner to a thief hates his own soul; he receives the oath but does not testify.

**v25** The fear of man is a snare, but whoever trusts in the LORD is set securely on high.

**v26** Many seek the ruler's favor, but a man receives justice from the LORD.

**v27** An unjust man is detestable to the righteous, and one whose way is upright is detestable to the wicked.
[^1]: Or who taxes heavily or who takes bribes ( 29:4)
[^2]: Or but the upright seek his soul ( 29:10)

### Chapter 30

#### The Words of Agur
**v1** These are the words of Agur son of Jakeh—the burden that this man declared to Ithiel: "I am weary, O God, and worn out. [^1]
**v2** Surely I am the most ignorant of men, and I lack the understanding of a man.
**v3** I have not learned wisdom, and I have no knowledge of the Holy One.
**v4** Who has ascended to heaven and come down?Who has gathered the wind in His hands?Who has bound up the waters in His cloak?Who has established all the ends of the earth?What is His name, and what is the name of His Son—surely you know!
**v5** Every word of God is flawless; He is a shield to those who take refuge in Him.
**v6** Do not add to His words, lest He rebuke you and prove you a liar.

**v7** Two things I ask of You—do not refuse me before I die:
**v8** Keep falsehood and deceitful words far from me.Give me neither poverty nor riches; feed me with the bread that is my portion.
**v9** Otherwise, I may have too muchand deny You, saying, 'Who is the LORD?' Or I may become poor and steal, profaning the name of my God.

**v10** Do not slander a servant to his master, or he will curse you, and you will bear the guilt.

**v11** There is a generation of those who curse their fathersand do not bless their mothers.
**v12** There is a generation of those who are pure in their own eyesand yet unwashed of their filth.
**v13** There is a generation—how haughty are their eyesand pretentious are their glances—
**v14** there is a generation whose teeth are swordsand whose jaws are knives, devouring the oppressed from the earthand the needy from among men.

**v15** The leech has two daughters:Give and Give.There are three things that are never satisfied, four that never say, 'Enough!':

**v16** Sheol, the barren womb, land never satisfied with water, and fire that never says, 'Enough!'

**v17** As for the eye that mocks a fatherand scorns obedience to a mother, may the ravens of the valley pluck it outand young vultures devour it.

**v18** There are three things too wonderful for me, four that I cannot understand:

**v19** the way of an eagle in the sky, the way of a snake on a rock, the way of a ship at sea, and the way of a man with a maiden.

**v20** This is the way of an adulteress:She eats and wipes her mouthand says, 'I have done nothing wrong.'

**v21** Under three things the earth trembles, under four it cannot bear up:

**v22** a servant who becomes king, a fool who is filled with food,

**v23** an unloved woman who marries, and a maidservant who supplants her mistress.

**v24** Four things on earth are small, yet they are exceedingly wise:

**v25** The ants are creatures of little strength, yet they store up their food in the summer;

**v26** the rock badgers [^2] are creatures of little power, yet they make their homes in the rocks;

**v27** the locusts have no king, yet they all advance in formation;

**v28** and the lizard can be caught in one's hands, yet it is found in the palaces of kings.

**v29** There are three things that are stately in their stride, and four that are impressive in their walk:

**v30** a lion, mighty among beasts, refusing to retreat before anything;

**v31** a strutting rooster; a he-goat; and a king with his army around him. [^3]

**v32** If you have foolishly exalted yourselfor if you have plotted evil, put your hand over your mouth.
**v33** For as the churning of milk yields butter, and the twisting of the nose draws blood, so the stirring of anger brings forth strife."
[^1]: Or declared to Ithiel: "I am weary, O God, but I can prevail. (revocalizations); Hebrew declared to Ithiel—to Ithiel and Ucal: ( 30:1)
[^2]: Or the coneys or the hyraxes ( 30:26)
[^3]: Or a king against whom there is no rising up ( 30:31)

### Chapter 31

#### The Sayings for King Lemuel
**v1** These are the words of King Lemuel—the burden that his mother taught him:

**v2** What shall I say, [^1] O my son?What, O son of my womb?What, O son of my vows?
**v3** Do not spend your strength on womenor your vigor on those who ruin kings.
**v4** It is not for kings, O Lemuel, it is not for kings to drink wine, or for rulers to crave strong drink,
**v5** lest they drink and forget what is decreed, depriving all the oppressed of justice.

**v6** Give strong drink to one who is perishing, and wine to the bitter in soul.
**v7** Let him drink and forget his poverty, and remember his misery no more.

**v8** Open your mouth for those with no voice, for the cause of all the dispossessed.
**v9** Open your mouth, judge righteously, and defend the cause of the poor and needy.
#### The Virtues of a Noble Woman

**v10** A wife [^2] of noble character, who can find?She is far more precious than rubies.

**v11** The heart of her husband trusts in her, and he lacks nothing of value.
**v12** She brings him good and not harmall the days of her life.
**v13** She selects wool and flaxand works with eager hands.
**v14** She is like the merchant ships, bringing her food from afar.

**v15** She rises while it is still nightto provide food for her householdand portions for her maidservants.
**v16** She appraises a field and buys it; from her earnings she plants a vineyard.
**v17** She girds herself [^3] with strengthand shows that her arms are strong.
**v18** She sees that her gain is good, and her lamp is not extinguished at night.
**v19** She stretches out her hands to the distaffand grasps the spindle with her fingers.

**v20** She opens her arms to the poorand reaches out her hands to the needy.
**v21** When it snows, she has no fear for her household, for they are all clothed in scarlet. [^4]
**v22** She makes coverings for her bed; her clothing is fine linen and purple.
**v23** Her husband is known at the city gates, where he sits among the elders of the land.
**v24** She makes linen garments and sells them; she delivers sashes to the merchants.

**v25** Strength and honor are her clothing, and she can laugh at the days to come.
**v26** She opens her mouth with wisdom, and faithful instruction is on her tongue.
**v27** She watches over the affairs of her householdand does not eat the bread of idleness.
**v28** Her children rise up and call her blessed; her husband praises her as well:
**v29** "Many daughters have done noble things, but you surpass them all!"

**v30** Charm is deceptive and beauty is fleeting, but a woman who fears the LORD is to be praised.
**v31** Give her the fruit of her hands, and let her works praise her at the gates.
[^1]: Or What or What are you doing ( 31:2)
[^2]: Verses 10–31 are an acrostic poem, each verse beginning with the successive letters of the Hebrew alphabet. ( 31:10)
[^3]: Hebrew She girds her loins ( 31:17)
[^4]: Or doubly clothed ( 31:21)

## Ecclesiastes

### Chapter 1

#### Everything Is Futile
**v1** These are the words of the Teacher, [^1] the son of David, king in Jerusalem:

**v2** "Futility [^2] of futilities,"says the Teacher,"futility of futilities!Everything is futile!"

**v3** What does a man gain from all his labor, at which he toils under the sun?
**v4** Generations come and generations go, but the earth remains forever.
**v5** The sun rises and the sun sets; it hurries back to where it rises.
**v6** The wind blows southward, then turns northward; round and round it swirls, ever returning on its course.
**v7** All the rivers flow into the sea, yet the sea is never full; to the place from which the streams come, there again they flow.

**v8** All things are wearisome, more than one can describe; the eye is not satisfied with seeing, nor the ear content with hearing.
**v9** What has been will be again, and what has been done will be done again; there is nothing new under the sun.
**v10** Is there a case where one can say,"Look, this is new"?It has already existedin the ages before us.
**v11** There is no remembranceof those who came before, and those yet to come will not be rememberedby those who follow after.
#### With Wisdom Comes Sorrow

**v12** I, the Teacher, was king over Israel in Jerusalem.
**v13** And I set my mind to seek and explore by wisdom all that is done under heaven. What a miserable task God has laid upon the sons of men to occupy them!

**v14** I have seen all the things that are done under the sun, and have found them all to be futile, a pursuit of the wind.

**v15** What is crooked cannot be straightened, and what is lacking cannot be counted.

**v16** I said to myself, "Behold, I have grown and increased in wisdom beyond all those before me who were over Jerusalem, and my mind has observed a wealth of wisdom and knowledge."

**v17** So I set my mind to know wisdom and madness and folly; I learned that this, too, is a pursuit of the wind.

**v18** For with much wisdom comes much sorrow, and as knowledge grows, grief increases.
[^1]: Or the Convener or the Preacher or the leader of the assembly; Hebrew Qoheleth is rendered as the Teacher throughout Ecclesiastes. ( 1:1)
[^2]: Literally vapor or breath; the Hebrew words translated in Ecclesiastes as forms of futile or fleeting can also be translated as vanity or meaningless. ( 1:2)

### Chapter 2

#### The Futility of Pleasure
**v1** I said to myself, "Come now, I will test you with pleasure; enjoy what is good!" But it proved to be futile.

**v2** I said of laughter, "It is folly," and of pleasure, "What does it accomplish?"

**v3** I sought to cheer my body with wine and to embrace folly—my mind still guiding me with wisdom—until I could see what was worthwhile for men to do under heaven during the few days of their lives.

**v4** I expanded my pursuits. I built houses and planted vineyards for myself.
**v5** I made gardens and parks for myself, where I planted all kinds of fruit trees.
**v6** I built reservoirs to water my groves of flourishing trees.

**v7** I acquired menservants and maidservants, and servants were born in my house. I also owned more herds and flocks than anyone in Jerusalem before me,
**v8** and I accumulated for myself silver and gold and the treasure of kings and provinces. I gathered to myself male and female singers, and the delights of the sons of men—many concubines.

**v9** So I became great and surpassed all in Jerusalem who had preceded me; and my wisdom remained with me.
**v10** Anything my eyes desired, I did not deny myself. I refused my heart no pleasure. For my heart took delight in all my work, and this was the reward for all my labor.

**v11** Yet when I considered all the works that my hands had accomplished and what I had toiled to achieve, I found everything to be futile, a pursuit of the wind; there was nothing to be gained under the sun.
#### The Wise and the Foolish

**v12** Then I turned to consider wisdom and madness and folly; for what more can the king's successor do than what has already been accomplished?
**v13** And I saw that wisdom exceeds folly, just as light exceeds darkness:

**v14** The wise man has eyes in his head, but the fool walks in darkness.Yet I also came to realize that one fate overcomes them both.
**v15** So I said to myself, "The fate of the fool will also befall me. What then have I gained by being wise?" And I said to myself that this too is futile.

**v16** For there is no lasting remembrance of the wise, just as with the fool, seeing that both will be forgotten in the days to come. Alas, the wise man will die just like the fool!
**v17** So I hated life, because the work that is done under the sun was grievous to me. For everything is futile and a pursuit of the wind.
#### The Futility of Work

**v18** I hated all for which I had toiled under the sun, because I must leave it to the man who comes after me.
**v19** And who knows whether that man will be wise or foolish? Yet he will take over all the labor at which I have worked skillfully under the sun. This too is futile.

**v20** So my heart began to despair over all the labor that I had done under the sun.
**v21** When there is a man who has labored with wisdom, knowledge, and skill, and he must give his portion to a man who has not worked for it, this too is futile and a great evil.
**v22** For what does a man get for all the toil and striving with which he labors under the sun?
**v23** Indeed, all his days are filled with grief, and his task is sorrowful; even at night, his mind does not rest. This too is futile.

**v24** Nothing is better for a man than to eat and drink and enjoy his work. I have also seen that this is from the hand of God.
**v25** For apart from Him, [^1] who can eat and who can find enjoyment?
**v26** To the man who is pleasing in His sight, He gives wisdom and knowledge and joy, but to the sinner He assigns the task of gathering and accumulating that which he will hand over to one who pleases God. This too is futile and a pursuit of the wind.
[^1]: Some Hebrew manuscripts, LXX, Syriac; most Hebrew manuscripts apart from me or more than I ( 2:25)

### Chapter 3

#### To Everything There Is a Season
**v1** To everything there is a season, and a time for every purpose under heaven:
**v2** a time to be born and a time to die, a time to plant and a time to uproot,
**v3** a time to kill and a time to heal, a time to break down and a time to build,
**v4** a time to weep and a time to laugh, a time to mourn and a time to dance,
**v5** a time to cast away stones and a time to gather stones together, a time to embrace and a time to refrain from embracing,
**v6** a time to search and a time to count as lost, a time to keep and a time to discard,
**v7** a time to tear and a time to mend, a time to be silent and a time to speak,
**v8** a time to love and a time to hate, a time for war and a time for peace.
#### God's Works Remain Forever

**v9** What does the worker gain from his toil?
**v10** I have seen the burden that God has laid upon the sons of men to occupy them.
**v11** He has made everything beautiful in its time. He has also set eternity in the hearts of men, yet they cannot fathom the work that God has done from beginning to end.

**v12** I know that there is nothing better for them than to rejoice and do good while they live,
**v13** and also that every man should eat and drink and find satisfaction in all his labor—this is the gift of God.
**v14** I know that everything God does endures forever; nothing can be added to it or taken from it. God does it so that they should fear Him.
**v15** What exists has already been, and what will be has already been, for God will call to account what has passed.
#### From Dust to Dust

**v16** Furthermore, I saw under the sun that in the place of judgment there is wickedness, and in the place of righteousness there is wickedness.
**v17** I said in my heart, "God will judge the righteous and the wicked, since there is a time for every activity and every deed."

**v18** I said to myself, "As for the sons of men, God tests them so that they may see for themselves that they are but beasts."
**v19** For the fates of both men and beasts are the same: As one dies, so dies the other—they all have the same breath. [^1] Man has no advantage over the animals, since everything is futile.
**v20** All go to one place; all come from dust, and all return to dust.

**v21** Who knows if the spirit of man rises upward and the spirit of the animal descends into the earth?
**v22** I have seen that there is nothing better for a man than to enjoy his work, because that is his lot. For who can bring him to see what will come after him?
[^1]: Or spirit ( 3:19)

### Chapter 4

#### The Evil of Oppression
**v1** Again I looked, and I considered all the oppression taking place under the sun. I saw the tears of the oppressed, and they had no comforter; the power lay in the hands of their oppressors, and there was no comforter.
**v2** So I admired the dead, who had already died, above the living, who are still alive.
**v3** But better than both is he who has not yet existed, who has not seen the evil that is done under the sun.

**v4** I saw that all labor and success spring from a man's envy of his neighbor. This too is futile and a pursuit of the wind.

**v5** The fool folds his handsand consumes his own flesh.
**v6** Better one handful with tranquilitythan two handfuls with toil and pursuit of the wind.

**v7** Again, I saw futility under the sun.
**v8** There is a man all alone, without even a son or brother. And though there is no end to his labor, his eyes are still not content with his wealth: "For whom do I toil and bereave my soul of enjoyment?" This too is futile—a miserable task.

**v9** Two are better than one, because they have a good return for their labor.
**v10** For if one falls down, his companion can lift him up; but pity the one who falls without another to help him up!
**v11** Again, if two lie down together, they will keep warm; but how can one keep warm alone?
**v12** And though one may be overpowered, two can resist. Moreover, a cord of three strands is not quickly broken.
#### The Futility of Power

**v13** Better is a poor but wise youth than an old but foolish king who no longer knows how to take a warning.
**v14** For the youth has come from the prison to the kingship, though he was born poor in his own kingdom.

**v15** I saw that all who lived and walked under the sun followed this second one, the youth who succeeded the king.
**v16** There is no limit to all the people who were before them. Yet the successor will not be celebrated by those who come even later. This too is futile and a pursuit of the wind.
### Chapter 5

#### Approaching God with Awe
**v1** Guard your steps when you go to the house of God. Draw near to listen rather than to offer the sacrifice of fools, who do not know that they do wrong.
**v2** Do not be quick to speak, and do not be hasty in your heart to utter a word before God. For God is in heaven and you are on earth. So let your words be few.
**v3** As a dream comes through many cares, so the speech of a fool comes with many words.

**v4** When you make a vow to God, do not delay in fulfilling it, because He takes no pleasure in fools. Fulfill your vow.
**v5** It is better not to vow than to make a vow and not fulfill it.

**v6** Do not let your mouth cause your flesh to sin, and do not tell the messenger [^1] that your vow was a mistake. Why should God be angry with your words and destroy the work of your hands?
**v7** For as many dreams bring futility, so do many words. Therefore, fear God.
#### The Futility of Wealth

**v8** If you see the oppression of the poor and the denial of justice and righteousness in the province, do not be astonished at the matter; for one official is watched by a superior, and others higher still are over them.
**v9** The produce of the earth is taken by all; the king himself profits from the fields.

**v10** He who loves money is never satisfied by money, and he who loves wealth is never satisfied by income. This too is futile.
**v11** When good things increase, so do those who consume them; what then is the profit to the owner, except to behold them with his eyes?

**v12** The sleep of the worker is sweet, whether he eats little or much, but the abundance of the rich man permits him no sleep.

**v13** There is a grievous evil I have seen under the sun: wealth hoarded to the harm of its owner,
**v14** or wealth lost in a failed venture, so when that man has a son there is nothing to pass on.

**v15** As a man came from his mother's womb, so he will depart again, naked as he arrived. He takes nothing for his labor to carry in his hands.
**v16** This too is a grievous affliction: Exactly as a man is born, so he will depart. What does he gain as he toils for the wind?
**v17** Moreover, all his days he eats in darkness, with much sorrow, sickness, and anger.

**v18** Here is what I have seen to be good and fitting: to eat and drink, and to find satisfaction in all the labor one does under the sun during the few days of life that God has given him—for this is his lot.

**v19** Furthermore, God has given riches and wealth to every man, and He has enabled him to enjoy them, to accept his lot, and to rejoice in his labor. This is a gift from God.
**v20** For a man seldom considers the days of his life, because God keeps him occupied with the joy of his heart.
[^1]: Or angel ( 5:6)

### Chapter 6

#### The Futility of Life
**v1** There is another evil I have seen under the sun, and it weighs heavily upon mankind:
**v2** God gives a man riches, wealth, and honor, so that he lacks nothing his heart desires; but God does not allow him to enjoy them. Instead, a stranger will enjoy them. This is futile and a grievous affliction.

**v3** A man may father a hundred children and live for many years; yet no matter how long he lives, if he is unsatisfied with his prosperity and does not even receive a proper burial, I say that a stillborn child is better off than he.
**v4** For a stillborn child enters in futility and departs in darkness, and his name is shrouded in obscurity.
**v5** The child, though neither seeing the sun nor knowing anything, has more rest than that man,
**v6** even if he lives a thousand years twice over but fails to enjoy his prosperity. Do not all go to the same place?

**v7** All a man's labor is for his mouth, yet his appetite is never satisfied. [^1]

**v8** What advantage, then, has the wise man over the fool? What gain comes to the poor man who knows how to conduct himself before others?
**v9** Better what the eye can see than the wandering of desire. This too is futile and a pursuit of the wind.

**v10** Whatever exists was named long ago, and it is known what man is; but he cannot contend with one stronger than he.
**v11** For the more words, the more futility—and how does that profit anyone?
**v12** For who knows what is good for a man during the few days in which he passes through his fleeting life like a shadow? Who can tell a man what will come after him under the sun?
[^1]: Hebrew filled ( 6:7)

### Chapter 7

#### The Value of Wisdom
**v1** A good name is better than fine perfume, and one's day of death is better than his day of birth.
**v2** It is better to enter a house of mourningthan a house of feasting, since death is the end of every man, and the living should take this to heart.

**v3** Sorrow is better than laughter, for a sad countenance is good for the heart.
**v4** The heart of the wise is in the house of mourning, but the heart of fools is in the house of pleasure.

**v5** It is better to heed a wise man's rebukethan to listen to the song of fools.
**v6** For like the crackling of thorns under the pot, so is the laughter of the fool. This too is futile.

**v7** Surely extortion turns a wise man into a fool, and a bribe corrupts the heart.
**v8** The end of a matter is better than the beginning, and a patient spirit is better than a proud one.

**v9** Do not be quickly provoked in your spirit, for anger settles in the lap of a fool. [^1]
**v10** Do not say, "Why were the old days better than these?" For it is unwise of you to ask about this.

**v11** Wisdom, like an inheritance, is good, and it benefits those who see the sun.
**v12** For wisdom, like money, is a shelter, and the advantage of knowledgeis that wisdom preserves the life of its owner.

**v13** Consider the work of God:Who can straighten what He has bent?
**v14** In the day of prosperity, be joyful, but in the day of adversity, consider this:God has made one of these along with the other, so that a man cannot discoveranything that will come after him.
#### The Limits of Human Wisdom

**v15** In my futile life I have seen both of these:A righteous man perishing in his righteousness, and a wicked man living long in his wickedness.

**v16** Do not be overly righteous, and do not make yourself too wise. Why should you destroy yourself?
**v17** Do not be excessively wicked, and do not be a fool. Why should you die before your time?
**v18** It is good to grasp the one and not let the other slip from your hand. For he who fears God will follow both warnings. [^2]

**v19** Wisdom makes the wise manstronger than ten rulers in a city.
**v20** Surely there is no righteous man on earthwho does good and never sins.

**v21** Do not pay attention to every word that is spoken, or you may hear your servant cursing you.
**v22** For you know in your heart that many times you yourself have cursed others.

**v23** All this I tested by wisdom, saying, "I resolve to be wise." But it was beyond me.
**v24** What exists is out of reach and very deep. Who can fathom it?

**v25** I directed my mind to understand, to explore, to search out wisdom and explanations, and to understand the stupidity of wickedness and the folly of madness.
**v26** And I find more bitter than death the woman who is a snare, whose heart is a net, and whose hands are chains. The man who pleases God escapes her, but the sinner is ensnared.

**v27** "Behold," says the Teacher, "I have discovered this by adding one thing to another to find an explanation.
**v28** While my soul was still searching but not finding, among a thousand I have found one upright man, but among all these I have not found one such woman.
**v29** Only this have I found: I have discovered that God made mankind upright, but they have sought out many schemes."
[^1]: Hebrew in the bosom of fools ( 7:9)
[^2]: Or will avoid all extremes ( 7:18)

### Chapter 8

#### Obey the King
**v1** Who is like the wise man? Who knows the interpretation of a matter? A man's wisdom brightens his face, and the sternness of his face is changed.

**v2** Keep the king's command, I say, because of your oath before God.
**v3** Do not hasten to leave his presence, and do not persist in a bad cause, for he will do whatever he pleases.
**v4** For the king's word is supreme, and who can say to him, "What are you doing?"

**v5** Whoever keeps his command will come to no harm, and a wise heart knows the right time and procedure.
**v6** For there is a right time and procedure to every purpose, though a man's misery weighs heavily upon him.
**v7** Since no one knows what will happen, who can tell him what is to come?

**v8** As no man has power over the wind to contain it, so no one has authority over his day of death. As no one can be discharged in wartime, so wickedness will not release those who practice it.
**v9** All this I have seen, applying my mind to every deed that is done under the sun; there is a time when one man lords it over another to his own detriment.
#### Fear God

**v10** Then too, I saw the burial of the wicked who used to go in and out of the holy place, and they were praised [^1] in the city where they had done so. This too is futile.
**v11** When the sentence for a crime is not speedily executed, the hearts of men become fully set on doing evil.

**v12** Although a sinner does evil a hundred times and still lives long, yet I also know that it will go well with those who fear God, who are reverent in His presence.
**v13** Yet because the wicked do not fear God, it will not go well with them, and their days will not lengthen like a shadow.
#### God's Ways Are Mysterious

**v14** There is a futility that is done on the earth: There are righteous men who get what the actions of the wicked deserve, and there are wicked men who get what the actions of the righteous deserve. I say that this too is futile.

**v15** So I commended the enjoyment of life, because there is nothing better for a man under the sun than to eat and drink and be merry. For this joy will accompany him in his labor during the days of his life that God gives him under the sun.

**v16** When I applied my mind to know wisdom and to observe the task that one performs on the earth—though his eyes do not see sleep in the day or even in the night—
**v17** I saw every work of God, and that a man is unable to comprehend the work that is done under the sun. Despite his efforts to search it out, he cannot find its meaning; even if the wise man claims to know, he is unable to comprehend.
[^1]: Some Hebrew manuscripts, LXX, and Vulgate; most Hebrew manuscripts were soon forgotten ( 8:10)

### Chapter 9

#### Death Comes to Good and Bad
**v1** So I took all this to heart and concluded that the righteous and the wise, as well as their deeds, are in God's hands. Man does not know what lies ahead, whether love or hate.

**v2** It is the same for all: There is a common fate for the righteous and the wicked, for the good and the bad, [^1] for the clean and the unclean, for the one who sacrifices and the one who does not. As it is for the good, so it is for the sinner; as it is for the one who makes a vow, so it is for the one who refuses to take a vow.

**v3** This is an evil in everything that is done under the sun: There is one fate for everyone. Furthermore, the hearts of men are full of evil and madness while they are alive, and afterward they join the dead.

**v4** There is hope, however, for anyone who is among the living; for even a live dog is better than a dead lion.
**v5** For the living know that they will die, but the dead know nothing. They have no further reward, because the memory of them is forgotten.
**v6** Their love, their hate, and their envy have already vanished, and they will never again have a share in all that is done under the sun.
#### Enjoy Your Portion in This Life

**v7** Go, eat your bread with joy, and drink your wine with a cheerful heart, for God has already approved your works:
**v8** Let your garments always be white, and never spare the oil for your head.

**v9** Enjoy life with your beloved wife all the days of the fleeting [^2] life that God has given you under the sun—all your fleeting days. For this is your portion in life and in your labor under the sun.
**v10** Whatever you find to do with your hands, do it with all your might, for in Sheol, where you are going, there is no work or planning or knowledge or wisdom.

**v11** I saw something else under the sun: The race is not to the swift, nor the battle to the strong; neither is the bread to the wise, nor the wealth to the intelligent, nor the favor to the skillful. For time and chance happen to all.
**v12** For surely no man knows his time: Like fish caught in a cruel net or birds trapped in a snare, so men are ensnared in an evil time that suddenly falls upon them.
#### Wisdom Is Better than Strength

**v13** I have also seen this wisdom under the sun, and it was great to me:
**v14** There was a small city with few men. A mighty king came against it, surrounded it, and built large siege ramps against it.

**v15** Now a poor wise man was found in the city, and he saved the city by his wisdom. Yet no one remembered that poor man.
**v16** And I said, "Wisdom is better than strength, but the wisdom of the poor man is despised, and his words are not heeded."

**v17** The calm words of the wise are heededover the shouts of a ruler among fools.
**v18** Wisdom is better than weapons of war, but one sinner destroys much good.
[^1]: LXX, Syriac, and Vulgate; Hebrew does not include and the bad. ( 9:2)
[^2]: Or futile; twice in this verse ( 9:9)

### Chapter 10

#### Wisdom and Folly
**v1** As dead flies bring a stench to the perfumer's oil, so a little folly outweighs wisdom and honor.
**v2** A wise man's heart inclines to the right, but the heart of a fool to the left.
**v3** Even as the fool walks along the road, his sense is lacking, and he shows everyone that he is a fool.
**v4** If the ruler's temper flares against you, do not abandon your post, for calmness lays great offenses to rest.

**v5** There is an evil I have seen under the sun—an error that proceeds from the ruler:
**v6** Folly is appointed to great heights, but the rich sit in lowly positions.
**v7** I have seen slaves on horseback, while princes go on foot like slaves.

**v8** He who digs a pit may fall into it, and he who breaches a wall may be bitten by a snake.
**v9** The one who quarries stones may be injured by them, and he who splits logs endangers himself.
**v10** If the axe is dull and the blade unsharpened, more strength must be exerted, but skill produces success.
**v11** If the snake bites before it is charmed, there is no profit for the charmer.

**v12** The words of a wise man's mouth are gracious, but the lips of a fool consume him.
**v13** The beginning of his talk is folly, and the end of his speech is evil madness.
**v14** Yet the fool multiplies words.No one knows what is coming, and who can tell him what will come after him?
**v15** The toil of a fool wearies him, for he does not know the way to the city.

**v16** Woe to you, O land whose king is a youth, [^1] and whose princes feast in the morning.
**v17** Blessed are you, O land whose king is a son of nobles, and whose princes feast at the proper time—for strength and not for drunkenness.

**v18** Through laziness the roof caves in, and in the hands of the idle, the house leaks.

**v19** A feast is prepared for laughter, and wine makes life merry, but money is the answer for everything.

**v20** Do not curse the king even in your thoughts, or curse the rich even in your bedroom, for a bird of the air may carry your words, and a winged creature may report your speech.
[^1]: Or a servant ( 10:16)

### Chapter 11

#### Cast Your Bread upon the Waters
**v1** Cast your bread upon the waters, for after many days you will find it again.
**v2** Divide your portion among seven, or even eight, for you do not know what disaster may befall the land.

**v3** If the clouds are full, they will pour out rain upon the earth; whether a tree falls to the south or to the north, in the place where it falls, there it will lie.
**v4** He who watches the wind will fail to sow, and he who observes the clouds will fail to reap.

**v5** As you do not know the path of the wind, or how the bones are formed [^1] in a mother's womb, so you cannot understand the work of God, the Maker of all things.
**v6** Sow your seed in the morning, and do not rest your hands in the evening, for you do not know which will succeed, whether this or that, or if both will equally prosper.
#### Enjoy Your Years

**v7** Light is sweet, and it pleases the eyes to see the sun.
**v8** So if a man lives many years, let him rejoice in them all.But let him remember the days of darkness, for they will be many.Everything to come is futile.

**v9** Rejoice, O young man, while you are young, and let your heart be glad in the days of your youth.Walk in the ways of your heartand in the sight of your eyes, but know that for all these things God will bring you to judgment.
**v10** So banish sorrow from your heart, and cast off pain from your body, for youth and vigor are fleeting. [^2]
[^1]: Or As you do not know the way the spirit comes to the bones ( 11:5)
[^2]: Or futile ( 11:10)

### Chapter 12

#### Remember Your Creator
**v1** Remember your Creator in the days of your youth, before the days of adversity comeand the years approach of which you will say,"I find no pleasure in them,"
**v2** before the light of the sun, moon, and stars is darkened, and the clouds return after the rain,
**v3** on the day the keepers of the house trembleand the strong men stoop, when those grinding cease because they are fewand those watching through windows see dimly,
**v4** when the doors to the street are shutand the sound of the mill fades away, when one rises at the sound of a birdand all the daughters of song grow faint,
**v5** when men fear the heights and dangers of the road, when the almond tree blossoms, the grasshopper loses its spring, and the caper berry shrivels—for then man goes to his eternal homeand mourners walk the streets.

**v6** Remember Him before the silver cord is snappedand the golden bowl is crushed, before the pitcher is shattered at the springand the wheel is broken at the well,
**v7** before the dust returns to the ground from which it cameand the spirit returns to God who gave it.

**v8** "Futility of futilities," says the Teacher." Everything is futile!"
#### The Whole Duty of Man

**v9** Not only was the Teacher wise, but he also taught the people knowledge; he pondered, searched out, and arranged many proverbs.
**v10** The Teacher searched to find delightful sayings and to record accurate words of truth. [^1]

**v11** The words of the wise are like goads, and the anthologies of the masters are like firmly embedded nails driven by a single Shepherd. [^2]
**v12** And by these, my son, be further warned: There is no end to the making of many books, and much study wearies the body.

**v13** When all has been heard, the conclusion of the matter is this: Fear God and keep His commandments, because this is the whole duty of man.
**v14** For God will bring every deed into judgment, along with every hidden thing, whether good or evil.
[^1]: Or and sought to write what was upright and true ( 12:10)
[^2]: Or shepherd ( 12:11)

## Song of Songs

### Chapter 1

#### The Bride Confesses Her Love
**v1** This is Solomon's Song of Songs. [^1]
#### The Bride

**v2** Let him kiss me with the kisses of his mouth!For your love is more delightful than wine.
**v3** The fragrance of your perfume is pleasing; your name is like perfume poured out.No wonder the maidens adore you.

**v4** Take me away with you—let us hurry!May the king bring me to his chambers.The Friends We will rejoice and delight in you; we will praise your love more than wine.The Bride It is only right that they adore you.

**v5** I am dark, yet lovely, O daughters of Jerusalem, like the tents of Kedar, like the curtains of Solomon.
**v6** Do not stare because I am dark, for the sun has gazed upon me.My mother's sons were angry with me; they made me a keeper of the vineyards, but my own vineyard I have neglected.

**v7** Tell me, O one I love, where do you pasture your sheep?Where do you rest them at midday?Why should I be like a veiled womanbeside the flocks of your companions?
#### The Friends

**v8** If you do not know, O fairest of women, follow the tracks of the flock, and graze your young goatsnear the tents of the shepherds.
#### The Bridegroom

**v9** I compare you, my darling, to a mare among Pharaoh's chariots.
**v10** Your cheeks are beautiful with ornaments, your neck with strings of jewels.
#### The Friends

**v11** We will make you ornaments of gold, studded with beads of silver.
#### The Bride

**v12** While the king was at his table, my perfume spread its fragrance.
**v13** My beloved is to me a sachet of myrrhresting between my breasts.
**v14** My beloved is to me a cluster of henna blossomsin the vineyards of En-gedi.
#### The Bridegroom

**v15** How beautiful you are, my darling!Oh, how very beautiful!Your eyes are like doves.
#### The Bride

**v16** How handsome you are, my beloved!Oh, how delightful!The soft grass is our bed.
#### The Bridegroom

**v17** The beams of our house are cedars; our rafters are fragrant firs.
[^1]: Most translators add subheadings for speaker identifications such as The Bride, The Groom, and The Friends based on the gender and number of the Hebrew words. ( 1:1)

### Chapter 2

#### The Bride's Admiration
#### The Bride

**v1** I am a rose of Sharon, [^1] a lily of the valley.
#### The Bridegroom

**v2** Like a lily among the thornsis my darling among the maidens.
#### The Bride

**v3** Like an apple tree among the trees of the forestis my beloved among the young men.I delight to sit in his shade, and his fruit is sweet to my taste.
**v4** He has brought me to the house of wine, [^2] and his banner over me is love.

**v5** Sustain me with raisins; refresh me with apples, for I am faint with love.

**v6** His left hand is under my head, and his right arm embraces me.
**v7** O daughters of Jerusalem, I adjure youby the gazelles and does of the field:Do not arouse or awaken loveuntil the time is right.

**v8** Listen! My beloved approaches.Look! Here he comes, leaping across the mountains, bounding over the hills.
**v9** My beloved is like a gazelle or a young stag.Look, he stands behind our wall, gazing through the windows, peering through the lattice.

**v10** My beloved calls to me,"Arise, my darling.Come away with me, my beautiful one.
**v11** For now the winter is past; the rain is over and gone.
**v12** The flowers have appeared in the countryside; the season of singing [^3] has come, and the cooing of turtledovesis heard in our land.
**v13** The fig tree ripens its figs; the blossoming vines spread their fragrance.Arise, come away, my darling; come away with me, my beautiful one."
#### The Bridegroom

**v14** O my dove in the clefts of the rock, in the crevices of the cliff, let me see your face, let me hear your voice; for your voice is sweet, and your countenance is lovely.
#### The Friends

**v15** Catch for us the foxes—the little foxes that ruin the vineyards—for our vineyards are in bloom.
#### The Bride

**v16** My beloved is mine and I am his; he pastures his flock among the lilies.
**v17** Before the day breaks and shadows flee, turn, my beloved, and be like a gazelleor a young stag on the mountains of Bether. [^4]
[^1]: Sharon Plain is a region in the coastal plain of Israel ( 2:1)
[^2]: That is, the banquet hall ( 2:4)
[^3]: Or pruning ( 2:12)
[^4]: Or the rugged mountains ( 2:17)

### Chapter 3

#### The Bride's Dream
**v1** On my bed at night I sought the one I love; I sought him, but did not find him.
**v2** I will arise now and go about the city, through the streets and squares.I will seek the one I love.So I sought him but did not find him.

**v3** I encountered the watchmen on their rounds of the city: "Have you seen the one I love?"
**v4** I had just passed them when I found the one I love.I held him and would not let gountil I had brought him to my mother's house, to the chamber of the one who conceived me.

**v5** O daughters of Jerusalem, I adjure youby the gazelles and does of the field:Do not arouse or awaken loveuntil the time is right.
#### Solomon Arrives on His Wedding Day

**v6** Who is this coming up from the wildernesslike a column of smoke, scented with myrrh and frankincensefrom all the spices of the merchant?
**v7** Behold, it is Solomon's carriage, [^1] escorted by sixty of the mightiest men of Israel.
**v8** All are skilled with the sword, experienced in warfare.Each has his sword at his sideprepared for the terror of the night.

**v9** King Solomon has made his carriageout of the timber of Lebanon.
**v10** He has made its posts of silver, its base of gold, its seat of purple fabric.Its interior is inlaid with loveby the daughters of Jerusalem.

**v11** Come out, O daughters of Zion, and gaze at King Solomon, wearing the crown with which his mother crowned himon the day of his wedding—the day of his heart's rejoicing.
[^1]: That is, the couch on which servants carry a king ( 3:7)

### Chapter 4

#### Solomon Admires His Bride
#### The Bridegroom

**v1** How beautiful you are, my darling—how very beautiful!Your eyes are like dovesbehind your veil.Your hair is like a flock of goatsstreaming down Mount Gilead.
**v2** Your teeth are like a flock of newly shorn sheepcoming up from the washing; each has its twin, and not one of them is lost.
**v3** Your lips are like a scarlet ribbon, and your mouth is lovely.Your brow behind your veilis like a slice of pomegranate.
**v4** Your neck is like the tower of David, built with rows of stones; on it hang a thousand shields, all of them shields of warriors.
**v5** Your breasts are like two fawns, twins of a gazelle grazing among the lilies.
