**v6** Before the day breaks and the shadows flee, I will make my wayto the mountain of myrrhand to the hill of frankincense.
**v7** You are altogether beautiful, my darling; in you there is no flaw.

**v8** Come with me from Lebanon, my bride, come with me from Lebanon!Descend [^1] from the peak of Amana, from the summits of Senir and Hermon, from the dens of the lions, from the mountains of the leopards.
**v9** You have captured my heart, my sister, my bride; you have stolen my heart with one glance of your eyes, with one jewel of your neck.
**v10** How delightful is your love, my sister, my bride!Your love is much better than wine, and the fragrance of your perfume than all spices.
**v11** Your lips, my bride, drip sweetness like the honeycomb; honey and milk are under your tongue, and the fragrance of your garmentsis like the aroma of Lebanon.

**v12** My sister, my bride, you are a garden locked up, a spring enclosed, a fountain sealed.
**v13** Your branches are an orchard of pomegranateswith the choicest of fruits, with henna and nard,
**v14** with nard and saffron, with calamus and cinnamon, with every kind of frankincense tree, with myrrh and aloes, with all the finest spices.
**v15** You are a garden spring, a well of fresh water [^2] flowing down from Lebanon.
#### The Bride

**v16** Awake, O north wind, and come, O south wind.Breathe on my gardenand spread the fragrance of its spices.Let my beloved come into his gardenand taste its choicest fruits.
[^1]: Or Look down ( 4:8)
[^2]: Or flowing water or living water ( 4:15)

### Chapter 5

#### The Bride and Her Beloved
#### The Bridegroom

**v1** I have come to my garden, my sister, my bride; I have gathered my myrrh with my spice.I have eaten my honeycomb with my honey; I have drunk my wine with my milk.The Friends Eat, O friends, and drink; drink freely, O beloved.
#### The Bride

**v2** I sleep, but my heart is awake.A sound! My beloved is knocking: "Open to me, my sister, my darling, my dove, my flawless one.My head is drenched with dew, my hair with the dampness of the night."

**v3** I have taken off my robe—must I put it back on?I have washed my feet—must I soil them again?
**v4** My beloved put his hand to the latch; my heart pounded for him.
**v5** I rose up to open for my beloved.My hands dripped with myrrh, my fingers with flowing myrrhon the handles of the bolt.
**v6** I opened for my beloved, but he had turned and gone.My heart sank at his departure.I sought him but did not find him.I called, but he did not answer.

**v7** I encountered the watchmen on their rounds of the city.They beat me and bruised me; they took away my cloak, those guardians of the walls.
**v8** O daughters of Jerusalem, I adjure you, if you find my beloved, tell him I am sick with love.
#### The Friends

**v9** How is your beloved better than others, O most beautiful among women?How is your beloved better than another, that you charge us so?
#### The Bride

**v10** My beloved is dazzling and ruddy, outstanding among ten thousand.
**v11** His head is purest gold; his hair is wavy and black as a raven.
**v12** His eyes are like dovesbeside the streams of water, bathed in milkand mounted like jewels.
**v13** His cheeks are like beds of spice, towers of perfume.His lips are like lilies, dripping with flowing myrrh.
**v14** His arms are rods of goldset with beryl.His body is polished ivorybedecked with sapphires.
**v15** His legs are pillars of marbleset on bases of pure gold.His appearance is like Lebanon, as majestic as the cedars.
**v16** His mouth [^1] is most sweet; he is altogether lovely.This is my beloved, and this is my friend, O daughters of Jerusalem.
[^1]: Hebrew palate ( 5:16)

### Chapter 6

#### Together in the Garden
#### The Friends

**v1** Where has your beloved gone, O most beautiful among women?Which way has he turned?We will seek him with you.
#### The Bride

**v2** My beloved has gone down to his garden, to the beds of spices, to pasture his flock in the gardensand to gather lilies.
**v3** I belong to my beloved and he belongs to me; he pastures his flock among the lilies.
#### The Bridegroom

**v4** You are as beautiful, my darling, as Tirzah, as lovely as Jerusalem, as majestic as troops with banners.
**v5** Turn your eyes away from me, for they have overcome me.Your hair is like a flock of goatsstreaming down from Gilead.
**v6** Your teeth are like a flock of sheepcoming up from the washing; each has its twin, and not one of them is lost.
**v7** Your brow behind your veilis like a slice of pomegranate.

**v8** There are sixty queens and eighty concubines, and maidens without number,
**v9** but my dove, my perfect one, is unique, the favorite of the mother who bore her.The maidens see her and call her blessed; the queens and concubines sing her praises.
#### The Friends

**v10** Who is this who shines like the dawn, as fair as the moon, as bright as the sun, as majestic as the stars in procession?
#### The Bridegroom

**v11** I went down to the walnut groveto see the blossoms of the valley, to see if the vines were buddingor the pomegranates were in bloom.
**v12** Before I realized it, my desire had set meamong the royal chariots of my people. [^1]
#### The Friends

**v13** Come back, come back, O Shulammite!Come back, come back, that we may gaze upon you.The Bridegroom Why do you look at the Shulammite, as on the dance of Mahanaim [^2]?
[^1]: Or among the chariots of Amminadab ( 6:12)
[^2]: Or the dance of the two camps ( 6:13)

### Chapter 7

#### Admiration by the Bridegroom
**v1** How beautiful are your sandaled feet, O daughter of the prince!The curves of your thighs are like jewels, the handiwork of a master.
**v2** Your navel is a rounded goblet; it never lacks blended wine.Your waist is a mound of wheatencircled by the lilies.
**v3** Your breasts are like two fawns, twins of a gazelle.
**v4** Your neck is like a towermade of ivory; your eyes are like the pools of Heshbonby the gate of Bath-rabbim; your nose is like the tower of Lebanon, facing toward Damascus.
**v5** Your head crowns you like Mount Carmel, the hair of your head like purple threads; the king is captured in your tresses.

**v6** How fair and pleasant you are, O love, with your delights!
**v7** Your stature is like a palm tree; your breasts are clusters of fruit.
**v8** I said, "I will climb the palm tree; I will take hold of its fruit." May your breasts be like clusters of the vine, the fragrance of your breath like apples,
**v9** and your mouth [^1] like the finest wine.The Bride May it flow smoothly to my beloved, gliding gently over lips and teeth. [^2]

**v10** I belong to my beloved, and his desire is for me.
**v11** Come, my beloved, let us go to the countryside; let us spend the night among the wildflowers. [^3]

**v12** Let us go early to the vineyardsto see if the vine has budded, if the blossom has opened, if the pomegranates are in bloom—there I will give you my love.

**v13** The mandrakes send forth a fragrance, and at our door is every delicacy, new as well as old, that I have treasured up for you, my beloved.
[^1]: Hebrew palate ( 7:9)
[^2]: LXX, Syriac, and Vulgate; Hebrew gliding gently over lips as we sleep ( 7:9)
[^3]: Or among the henna blossoms or in the villages ( 7:11)

### Chapter 8

#### Longing for Her Beloved
**v1** O that you were to me like a brotherwho nursed at my mother's breasts!If I found you outdoors, I would kiss you, and no one would despise me.
**v2** I would lead you and bring youto the house of my mother who taught me.I would give you spiced wine to drink, the nectar of my pomegranates.

**v3** His left hand is under my head, and his right arm embraces me.
**v4** O daughters of Jerusalem, I adjure you:Do not arouse or awaken loveuntil the time is right.
#### The Friends

**v5** Who is this coming up from the wilderness, leaning on her beloved?The Bride I roused you under the apple tree; there your mother conceived you; there she travailed and brought you forth.

**v6** Set me as a seal over your heart, as a seal upon your arm.For love is as strong as death, its jealousy [^1] as unrelenting as Sheol.Its sparks are fiery flames, the fiercest blaze of all.
**v7** Mighty waters cannot quench love; rivers cannot sweep it away.If a man were to give all the wealth of his house for love, his offer would be utterly scorned.
#### The Friends

**v8** We have a little sister, and her breasts are not yet grown.What shall we do for our sisteron the day she is spoken for?
**v9** If she is a wall, we will build a tower of silver upon her.If she is a door, we will enclose her with panels of cedar.
#### The Bride

**v10** I am a wall, and my breasts are like towers.So I have become in his eyeslike one who brings peace.
**v11** Solomon had a vineyard in Baal-hamon.He leased it to the tenants.For its fruit, each was to bringa thousand shekels of silver. [^2]
**v12** But my own vineyard is mine to give; the thousand shekels are for you, O Solomon, and two hundred are for those who tend its fruit.
#### The Bridegroom

**v13** You who dwell in the gardens, my companions are listening for your voice.Let me hear it!
#### The Bride

**v14** Come away, my beloved, and be like a gazelleor a young stagon the mountains of spices.
[^1]: Or passion ( 8:6)
[^2]: Hebrew a thousand of silver; that is, approximately 25.1 pounds or 11.4 kilograms of silver ( 8:11)
